        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/31285891-perfect">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18967379-bookphenomena-micky?shelf=arc-read">arc-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18967379-bookphenomena-micky?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18967379-bookphenomena-micky?shelf=2017-read">2017-read</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1773108990" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11065486672433386780">This conclusion to the Flawed duet brought a fast-paced narrative from start to finish. The story of Celestine remained engaging as she navigated not only being Flawed but also being an evader and the most prominent Flawed ever known. Sitting at the heart of the read is prejudice and this theme resonates with any contemporary society, so all readers should be able to identify. What is compelling about this particular society under The Guild rule is, what happens to society when compassion, empat</span>
  <span id="freeText11065486672433386780" style="display:none">This conclusion to the Flawed duet brought a fast-paced narrative from start to finish. The story of Celestine remained engaging as she navigated not only being Flawed but also being an evader and the most prominent Flawed ever known. Sitting at the heart of the read is prejudice and this theme resonates with any contemporary society, so all readers should be able to identify. What is compelling about this particular society under The Guild rule is, what happens to society when compassion, empathy and kindness are only acceptable for the perfect. <br /><br />Celestine remained a mildly chaotic character, due to her age, her notoriety and need to mature quickly. Nevertheless, she had courage and strength. Carrick was much more prominent in PERFECT and I enjoyed having his character developed more and the relationship dynamics were compelling. The side characters were all strong and this wide cast of characters is what made this such a good read. <br /><br />Cecelia Ahern has demonstrated her YA and dystopian story-telling abilities with not only a first book but the ability to write a strong sequel. I will be looking out for similar work from her in the future.<br /><br />A copy of this book was provided by the publisher through netgalley, in return for a honest review.<br /><br />Reviewed for Jo&amp;IsaLoveBooks Blog.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1978767927" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1978767927" />
    <a title="chelsea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10373376-chelsea"><img alt="chelsea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451460177p2/10373376.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1978767927?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chelsea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chelsea" href="/user/show/10373376-chelsea">chelsea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1978767927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1746886392461516819">i read flawed in one sitting, i loved it so much. of course, perfect wasn’t disappointing in the slightest. i’m sad to see this duology end, but i’m also glad that it wasn’t dragged out like some series are, y’know?<br/><br/>i wasn’t a big fan of the romance in the first book. i didn’t like either love interests, and i felt that neither the romantic subplots nor the characters got the development the needed. they were just kinda there.<br/><br/>i love how perfect had a lot more action in it than flawed. it felt str</span>
  <span id="freeText1746886392461516819" style="display:none">i read flawed in one sitting, i loved it so much. of course, perfect wasn’t disappointing in the slightest. i’m sad to see this duology end, but i’m also glad that it wasn’t dragged out like some series are, y’know?<br /><br />i wasn’t a big fan of the romance in the first book. i didn’t like either love interests, and i felt that neither the romantic subplots nor the characters got the development the needed. they were just kinda there.<br /><br />i love how perfect had a lot more action in it than flawed. it felt strange to read initially because i was expecting something like flawed and more on the contemporary side of the dystopian genre, not so brutal. it was a good change.<br /><br />i loved celestine even more in perfect. she was more determined than before. she grew so much as a character, it’s hard not to like her. i wasn’t her biggest fan during the first book, but i’ve come to love her a lot over the 2 books. i’m a little disappointed with her sister – i’d expected more from her but i do like how she acted in the end. the family dynamic in this duology is amazing. many ya books seem to forget about family, especially the parents.<br /><br />another thing i really enjoyed about perfect was the flow from book 1 to 2. i read these books back to back and it felt like one big story rather than two separate books.<br /><br />the only thing that i didn’t like about this book is one of the last scenes that’s supposed to be empowering but came off more as self harm than anything. i won’t say what, for sake of spoilers, but i feel like the only one who’s felt this way towards the ending.<br /><br />overall, perfect was a phenomenal read and a great ending to a series. i hope more people read this book, as i don’t see any hype for it (and flawed definitely deserves it).</span>
  <a data-text-id="1746886392461516819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1653134478" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1653134478" />
    <a title="Daria Marshall" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21892859-daria-marshall"><img alt="Daria Marshall" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1450952957p2/21892859.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1653134478?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daria Marshall" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daria Marshall" href="/user/show/21892859-daria-marshall">Daria Marshall</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21892859-daria-marshall?shelf=diverse-reads-2k17">diverse-reads-2k17</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1653134478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer311119354235650870">3.5 stars<br/><br/>I wasn't the biggest fan of Flawed to begin with, but I was curious to see how the story ended up. I did think this was slightly better than Flawed, but it still missed the mark for me. <br/><br/>It still bothered me how many times Celestine repeated herself. Especially about being Flawed and having six brands and all of that jazz. It felt like I was being hit of the head with that information a couple of times. <br/><br/>I still don't see the chemistry between Celestine and Carrick. I also don't see the c</span>
  <span id="freeText311119354235650870" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />I wasn't the biggest fan of Flawed to begin with, but I was curious to see how the story ended up. I did think this was slightly better than Flawed, but it still missed the mark for me. <br /><br />It still bothered me how many times Celestine repeated herself. Especially about being Flawed and having six brands and all of that jazz. It felt like I was being hit of the head with that information a couple of times. <br /><br />I still don't see the chemistry between Celestine and Carrick. I also don't see the chemistry between Celestine and Art. I would have rather there was no romance at all, to be honest.<br /><br />But it was nice to see Celestine's family come back and play a bigger role. I especially liked Celestine's grandfather. I felt like he was one of the only characters that really had any substance to him. There were still times that I was incredibly frustrated with Celestine. But she did grow from the first book and she did learn from her mistakes. I was going to be really disappointed if she hadn't made some of the choices that she did because then it would have been just a repeat of the first one where she trusted everyone. <br /><br />I feel like this was a decent conclusion to the duology and I'm glad I read it. It just didn't wow me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="311119354235650870" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1953533350" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1953533350" />
    <a title="Chandra Claypool (wherethereadergrows)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9722719-chandra-claypool-wherethereadergrows"><img alt="Chandra Claypool (wherethereadergrows)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534358832p2/9722719.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1953533350?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chandra Claypool (wherethereadergrows)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chandra Claypool (wherethereadergrows)" href="/user/show/9722719-chandra-claypool-wherethereadergrows">Chandra Claypool (wherethereadergrows)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/31285891-perfect">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1953533350" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer832842433285194791">Celestine North is back. On the run, hiding from the Guild, she's on a mission to get her verdict revoked and get Judge Crevan accountable for his actions. She has one secret that could bring down the entire system. She's not entirely sure who she can trust as Flawed and non-Flawed have their own agendas. Decisions have to be made, lives depend on her. But every time she gains momentum, the tides turn on her again. Art, Carrick, Flawed, non-Flawed, her family, human rights for all - it's a lot o</span>
  <span id="freeText832842433285194791" style="display:none">Celestine North is back. On the run, hiding from the Guild, she's on a mission to get her verdict revoked and get Judge Crevan accountable for his actions. She has one secret that could bring down the entire system. She's not entirely sure who she can trust as Flawed and non-Flawed have their own agendas. Decisions have to be made, lives depend on her. But every time she gains momentum, the tides turn on her again. Art, Carrick, Flawed, non-Flawed, her family, human rights for all - it's a lot of weight on the shoulders of someone who just turned 18. <br /><br />I loved the continuation of Celestine's story. While YA dystopia novels pretty much run on the same tangent, it doesn't deter me from loving the story told a different way. And this is better than some I've read. Again, this entire story holds traces of the Scarlet Letter, human rights, segregation and bullying. I will say that I did like the first book better than this one, but that's not to say that this wasn't a fun read. It is fast paced and I was excited to see what was going to happen next. I'm so tired of love triangles and that played a little more in this book so I kind of sighed there. But hey, like I said, same tangent. Predictable, but fun. The concept is fantastic and I was happy with how the author ended this. Especially with giving a glimpse of "where are they now". Always a fan of that. Definitely think this and Flawed are well worth the read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="832842433285194791" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

      <span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_review_1953533350'><a id="like_count_review_1953533350" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1953533350?resource_type=Review"><span class="likesCount">6 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F28116714-perfect">Like</a></span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1884916689" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1884916689" />
    <a title="T.J. Burns" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23826579-t-j-burns"><img alt="T.J. Burns" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537432736p2/23826579.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1884916689?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="T.J. Burns" class="user" itemprop="url" name="T.J. Burns" href="/user/show/23826579-t-j-burns">T.J. Burns</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23826579-t-j-burns?shelf=2017-03-march">2017-03-march</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23826579-t-j-burns?shelf=young-adult-teen">young-adult-teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23826579-t-j-burns?shelf=fantasy-sci-fi">fantasy-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23826579-t-j-burns?shelf=preferred-publisher">preferred-publisher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23826579-t-j-burns?shelf=macmillan-childrens">macmillan-childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23826579-t-j-burns?shelf=ng">ng</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23826579-t-j-burns?shelf=owned-book">owned-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23826579-t-j-burns?shelf=netgalley-edelweiss-reviewed">netgalley-edelweiss-reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1884916689" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer790633323021548340"><i>Perfect</i> was a fantastic read! Everything I hope for in a book and more! Suspense, mystery, unexpected twists and turns, thought-provoking content, intelligent (and at time witty) dialogue, interesting/intriguing characters who experience character growth, and a splash of romance! <br/><br/>Ahern's writing style is brilliant. Following Celestine's thought process is amazing as she grows and develops, learns from her mistakes, questions the world around her and everything she's been taught to believe is tru</span>
  <span id="freeText790633323021548340" style="display:none"><i>Perfect</i> was a fantastic read! Everything I hope for in a book and more! Suspense, mystery, unexpected twists and turns, thought-provoking content, intelligent (and at time witty) dialogue, interesting/intriguing characters who experience character growth, and a splash of romance! <br /><br />Ahern's writing style is brilliant. Following Celestine's thought process is amazing as she grows and develops, learns from her mistakes, questions the world around her and everything she's been taught to believe is true, draws her own conclusions, overcomes betrayal, learns to trust.<br /><br />The varied chapter lengths works really well to move the story along, sometimes long to reveal a more in-depth analysis or detailed scene, sometime incredibly short to create a sense of urgency.<br /><br />I wish I hadn't had to wait a year to read this second book -- the two books would have flowed so seamlessly together. It seems more like one complete book than a duology, and the first book didn't really have an ending. I wondered if the two parts were actually written as one and then separated for marketing purposes.<br /><br />The two books together, <i>Flawed</i> and <i>Perfect</i> deal with a heavy subject matter, which in its presentation is dark enough, but at one point toward the end of the second book, Ahern alludes to an even darker possible turn of events (see spoiler below), which given the historical events of the not so distant past, would be entirely conceivable. <br /><br />We are presented with a system for regulating moral conduct – a Theocracy – with Judge Crevan (Bosco) as the infallible Executive Theocrat, the moral judge, the decider of right from wrong.<br /><br />We get introduced to this system by Celestine, a 17-year-old who was raised in this system and genuinely finds it to be a good way to keep people on the moral path. Celestine’s Granddad, Cornelius, and her sister, Juniper, are presented as critics of the system – the free-thinkers.<br /><br />It is essential for the story that we receive a description of this moral system from the perspective of an indoctrinated, like Celestine, rather than from someone who sets himself/herself critically towards the system, such as Juniper or Cornelius. <br /><br />The way in which Celestine first describes “the Guild” initially led me to believe it to be harmless. The more I learned about this system, the more I came to recognize it as a brutally oppressive theocratic dictatorship, which uses fear tactics, censorship, torture, imprisonment, ostracization, and stigmatization to force the majority to follow the moral edicts of a small minority. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />I had a big scare for a moment toward the end of the second book, and had to pause to decide whether to go on. <br /><br />The scene at the fish gutting hall, the women with blood red color all over their clothes... I couldn't believe the book would go that dark, but it was entirely possible. Genocide has happened in human history, so it is not as unthinkable as I would like to believe. <br /><br />Along with Celestine, I feared the worst. Could this be some kind of "Endlösung" -- some diabolical plan to get rid of all the flawed once and for all? It certainly wouldn't serve the purpose of the Guild, but Bosco in an anger-crazed mania may have attempted to get rid of the potential rebels and avert an impending rebellion. <br /><br />Thankfully, I didn't have to worry too long to be relieved of this notion -- and the march of the flawed in skimpy clothing was then a relief and not as shocking as it would have been otherwise.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><i>Perfect</i> shows the dangers of letting a theocratic dictatorship control our thoughts and actions, and stresses the importance (and mandate!) of following what our own consciences know to be "right," "just," compassionate," and "logical," even when the political and religious system set in place forbids such actions. <br /><br /><i>Perfect</i> is much more than an outward political critique, however. <i>Perfect</i> also looks inwardly, asking readers to celebrate all of our imperfections and encouraging us to accept ourselves as "perfect" just as we are -- perfection in balance with our flaws. <br /><br />Celestine concludes that we, "the flawed," can learn from the mistakes we've made, while "the unflawed" presumably haven't made any mistakes to learn from (at least none they are willing to admit to). Ergo, the flawed are a whole lot smarter, having learned a whole lot more. <br /><br /><i>Perfect</i> is intriguing, provocative, and exciting! It examines external moral structures, such as cults, theocracies, and ideological dictatorships with a condemning eye, and it denounces any society's attempt to hold its members (or any individual's attempt to hold himself/herself) to a "perfect" standard that does not include looking to our consciences for answers, acting with compassion, learning from our mistakes, and accepting ourselves with all of our imperfections as "perfect" -- just the way we are.<br /><br /><i>I received a copy of this book from Macmillan Children's Publishing Group via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.</i><br /><br />BUDDY READ: Dystopian/Sci-Fi &gt; Perfect (Flawed #2) by Cecelia Ahern - Starting February 15th 2017<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/18437680-perfect-flawed-2-by-cecelia-ahern---starting-february-15th-2017">https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="790633323021548340" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SKjCe/UK2ESHdhtAPtb4v1/9vO0ZL8TaokQQJuFTDz3L7OsiklDbCeccmKgoWQ5cKE8jEf12zeiOMP4c/sn1FA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3VJgAxvFz5D6vKzJaVu5Bb9Zu6Iq8ogtgYXnEW0Y/5leFklafJ/M3ZrWLyF/1E/myOskXs6rgR+t8QkrcoIFsA==')})
  }
//]]>

She is now published in nearly fifty countries, and has sold over twenty-five million copies of her novels worldwide. Two of her books have been adapted as films and she has created several TV series.</span>
